** THIS IS AN UNPUBLISHED DECISION - NOT INTENDED FOR CITATION AS PRECEDENT **
 
U.S. Department of Justice
Executive Office for Immigration Review
Board of Immigration Appeals
IN RE: ARLIND PRAPANIKU
File: AXX XX7 471 - Los Angeles
November 10, 2004
 
IN REMOVAL PROCEEDINGS
  
MOTION
 
 
ON BEHALF OF RESPONDENT:
 
James C. Angleton, Esquire
 
CHARGE:
 
*1 Notice: Sec. 237(a)(1)(B), I&N Act ¿8 U.S.C. § 1227(a)(1)(B)º - In the United States in violation of law
  
APPLICATION: Reconsideration
 
On January 21, 2004, the Board summarily affirmed the Immigration Judge’s decision. On August 6, 2004, the Board denied the respondent’s motion to reopen based upon ineffective assistance of his former counsel. The respondent has now filed a motion to reconsider. The Department of Homeland Security has not responded to the motion. In our August 6, 2004, decision we agreed that the respondent had complied with the requirements set forth in our decision in Matter of Lozada, 19 I&N Dec. 637 (BIA), aff’d, 857 F.2d 10 (1st Cir. 1988). In this regard, we note that former counsel was given an opportunity to respond to the respondent’s allegations, and he merely submitted a perfunctory denial stating, “I dispute your contentions and the allegations of your client about my ineffective assistance of counsel in my representation of him before the Immigration Court.” See Edguardo Quintanilla’s letter dated April 6, 2004, at Exhibit C attached to the motion.
 
In the motion to reconsider the respondent points out that subsequent to our August 6, 2004, decision, Maravilla v. Ashcroft, 381 F.3d 855, at 858 (9th Cir. 2004) (per curiam) (holding that the proper prejudice standard for an ineffective assistance of counsel claim, is “only whether ¿the attorney’sº deficient performance may have affected the proceedings.”) was decided. We shall grant the motion to reconsider in light of Maravilla v. Ashcroft. It appears that former counsel’s representation of the respondent prior to and during the removal hearing may have contributed to the Immigration Judge’s adverse credibility determination for the reasons contained in the respondent’s motion, and the allegations appear to be reflected in the record. Moreover, our assessment of the respondent’s allegations are enhanced by former counsel’s perfunctory response which did not explain why he disagreed with the respondent’s allegations. See Reyes v. Ashcroft, 358 F.3d 592, 599 (9th Cir.2004); Matter of Lozada, at 639.
 
ORDER: The motion to reconsider is granted, the removal proceedings are reopened, and the record is remanded to the Immigration Court for further proceedings.

2004 WL 2943594 (BIA)
 
** THIS IS AN UNPUBLISHED DECISION - NOT INTENDED FOR CITATION AS PRECEDENT **
 
U.S. Department of Justice
Executive Office for Immigration Review
Board of Immigration Appeals
IN RE: YU WANG YING
File: AXX XX9 432 - Los Angeles
November 9, 2004
 
IN REMOVAL PROCEEDINGS
  
MOTION
 
 
ON BEHALF OF RESPONDENT: Pro se
 
 
ORDER:
 
*1 PER CURIAM. On June 23, 2004, the Board dismissed the respondent’s appeal for lack of jurisdiction because it was untimely filed. We accordingly returned the record to the Immigration Court without further action. Now the respondent has filed a Correction to Motion to Reopen and Reconsider Exclusion Proceeding, Request for Acceptance of the Motion, which we will construe as a motion to reconsider due to the contents of the motion. The motion to reconsider will be denied.
 
The Board does not normally have jurisdiction over motions filed in cases where the Board never assumed initial jurisdiction, such as an untimely appeal. See Matter of Mladineo, 14 I&N Dec. 591 (BIA 1974). We retain jurisdiction over the instant motion to the extent that it challenges the finding of untimeliness or requests consideration of the reasons for untimeliness. See Matter of Lopez, 22 I&N Dec. 16 (BIA 1998).
 
A motion to reconsider asserts that at the time of the Board’s previous decision an error was made. It “questions the Board’s decision for alleged errors in appraising the facts and the law.” Matter of Cerna, 20 I&N Dec. 399 (BIA 1991). We note that the respondent in this case has established no error of law or fact in our prior decision. Rather, the respondent asserts that due to ineffective assistance of counsel, the appeal was untimely filed. However, we note that the respondent has offered no evidence to support this claim. Therefore, we need not address this issue of ineffective assistance and we decline to reconsider our prior decision where the respondent has established no error in that determination.
 
Accordingly, the motion to reconsider is denied.
  
<Signature>
  
FOR THE BOARD
 
2004 WL 2943594 (BIA)
End of Document
